<Author>elegantly_wasted22
<Content>A Mixed Impression of the Riu Florida Beach I stayed at the Riu Florida Beach in early July 2008 with my mother for two nights. It was our first time visiting Miami, and after reading some of the reviews of the hotel, we were a little apprehensive. First of all, the area that the hotel is situated in is not great - there are a lot of abandoned buildings across the street and although this is not the hotel's fault, it does affect the general impression of the place, and the view!! The lobby of the hotel is beautiful - large, cool and airy with plenty of seats. Check-in was.....time consuming. Staff, somewhat predictably, speak English as a second language so we had to wait for a member of staff to be free who had the best grasp of English before we could check in. We stayed on the seventh floor - the room was spacious and clean with all the expected amenities. Be warned though - the walls are paper-thin so if you have chatty neighbours then be prepared for a poor sleep!The breakfast buffet was large and well-stocked and the dining area was lovely. The pool area was also impressive - clean and plenty of sun loungers with shady areas and umbrellas too. The beach is right outside of the hotel so that can also be used as an alternative to the pool. Location is not perfect. The boardwalk is situated right outside of the hotel and this can be used to walk to the main restaurant/shopping area near Ocean Drive and lower Collins Ave - but it is a considerable walk. The area immediately surrounding the hotel has nothing in terms of entertainment/dining.

<Author>sjp84
<Content>We really enjoyed our stay! Well let's see now...Having read some of the reviews on here, I was really quite anxious about going to the Riu. However, everything was absolutely fine!1. The two lifts worked perfectly for the entire week we were there. Ok sometimes we had to wait a few minutes, but that was not an issue for us. (Patience and all that!) We also used the stairs quite a bit as only on the 5th floor.2. Definitely glad we paid extra for an ocean view room - well worth it. We looked straight out over the pool to the beach/ocean beyond. Lovely.3. The breakfast was nothing short of amazing. I can't even begin to list the food that was available. The choice was fantastic and could rival any 5* hotel I'm sure.4. All the staff we spoke to were very polite and helpful, particularly those behind the check-in desk. We had no problems at all.5. Location - ok so it is not on Ocean Drive and yes it is a little bit of a walk, but the boardwalk is lovely and it took us about 20/30 minutes to get into the main restaurant area. In the evenings we chose not to walk along the boardwalk, but along the main streets (out the front of the hotel) which again took about 20/30 minutes. We thought it was a really nice stroll before dinner, but if you are not into walking or find it difficult to walk for this amount of time, a taxi cost $7-8. This price is for coming in the other direction (centre to hotel) but I presume it will be the same from the hotel to Ocean Drive.6. The rooms could do with a little updating - new carpet, more contemporary bedding etc, but we don't go on holiday to stay in our hotel room. It was very clean, and got cleaned thoroughly every day too. Also fresh towels daily if needed.7. If you like a bit of retail therapy... we visited Aventura Mall by getting the 'S' bus straight outside the hotel. Definitely worth it!! The mall is fab with a huge selection of shops and a cinema complex. It cost $2 each, one-way and takes approx 45 minutes to get there. The buses come along frequently so you don't have to wait too long for one.We really enjoyed our stay at the Riu. Would possibly look for something nearer Ocean Drive next time, but would not hesitate to go back here.

<Author>Superhoteluser
<Content>Not bad for the price.... almost liked it a lot! Just spent 9 nights at the Riu Florida Beach hotel. Initially given room 631 but then upgraded to an ocean view room 1034 (well worth it for the balcony and the view!) My opinions are set out below....and just for the record, I think my standards are quite high.Good points:- Rooms are big and clean- In relation to the rest of Miami - the location of the hotel is in Miami Beach and not South Beach. I much preferred the location of the Riu to some of the South Beach hotels. The beach in front of the Riu is fab and not overcrowded. Bus stops to Lincoln Road and South Beach are a 1 minute walk away on Collins Ave. The bus to the north and Aventura Mall (highly recommended) is literally outside the hotel...so when you return from Lincoln Road or South Beach, you are dropped right outside the Riu's door. You get to see real 'America' when you take public transport.... we had several giggles and shocks on our bus journeys! Well worth it for $2 each.- Really great staff - all of them. Housekeeping, Reception, valet guys, tour provider, restaurant...all friendly and very helpful- Breakfasts have a large choice - not always the freshest, but lots to choose from- Rooms are tidied and cleaned to a good standard daily- Lifts worked 99% of the time, so had no concerns. - City/boat tour interesting - good photo and celeb spotting opportunitiesCould do better:- Cheaper bar drinks by the pool. We paid $9 for 2 small bottles of water- Rush for the sunbeds in the morning. If you don't have your towel out by 10.30am, you're unlikely to get a space by the pool (beach is better anyway!)- The colour of the bedspreads For anyone leaving from Miami International Airport on a british airways flight - their duty free area is rubbish. Much cheaper to buy cosmetics, makeup and liquor in Macy's or Liquor stores respectively.

<Author>Digby9
<Content>The Reviews are Bad for a Reason... My Partner and I stayed here in September 2008. Based on previous reviews, I do have to say that the hotel was better than I expected, but it is simply not up to standard and that's a fact that is not open to interpretation. The man behind reception took my Credit Card for any extras and then promptly disappeared out the back with my card for 5 minutes, which I was very unhappy about. I will be scrutinizing my credit card statement very carefully for the next few months. The hotel is 15 blocks from the start on South Beach life, which means a minimum 45 minute walk each way (unshaded, in 94 degree heat!). I had read previous reports that the lifts did not work, but both were working in September 2008, which was lucky as we were on 9th floor and would have flipped if we'd have to take the stairs. The room was okay, but I'm not sure the beds are doubles, more like large singles that don't sleep 2 people comfortably. The shower was very very basic, obviously a cheap shop attachment. Worryingly, the water pressure and temperature change without warning. Once, the water pressure literally dropped so such that it was dribbling out of the head and the temperature would go very high or low on it's own accord. Be very careful if you have children as our shower would also squirt water in every direction, chasing you around the bath with alternating scalding/freezing water. The pool area is great and breakfast cannot be criticised, the selection really was great. I would recommend staying at least 10 blocks further South and would be unlikely to stay here again. Heed the warnings of other contributors and you won't be disappointed.

<Author>Mr_B78
<Content>Mixed bag for the Riu Both lifts worked, we had a bathroom, we had a seaview, Most of the staff are really nice and helpfull, however a four star hotel?? I have stayed in better 3 stars. It was our honeymoon and also my birthday so we decieded to book what looked like the best hotel they had to offer in the agents. (I kind of wish i read this site first.)When we got there we were greeted very nicley and everything was easy and pleasant at check in, We even had a Dutch girl explaining everything in Dutch (where we live). Our room was an ocean view room on the tenth floor, we were lucky enough to have one of the two only king size beds. The room did smell of wet dog, I presume that is because of the humidity and leaking balcony door on the old stained carpet. The walk in wardorbe was nice and contained a fridge(without mini bar) and the safe (which costs 2 dollars per day) The bathroom was very basic and the bath was a bit dirty (This is not to say it hadnt been cleaned, just that it was old and needed replacing) The room just seemed to lack class, something that I would have expected. It was travelodge, without the fininshing touches, but with a balcony. The view if you stood looking in one direction is really good, but if you look staright forward you see a borded up old hotel with stagnant water and broken glass. An ocean view room is not the same as an ocean front room (something that we were never offered) It was our honemoon, so we were recomended this as a good honeymoon location. The second day we were given a bottle of Champangne and some fruit and a calander of south beach from the Manager. Most of the staff were really nice. But the hotel had no room service!, (a must on a honeymoon) and the snacks avalible down stairs, were limited over priced and lacking flair, but nice if you want burger and chips. The swiming pool is good and the beach is two minutes away. It is a 20 min walk from all the restuarants and shops, we didnt mind that too much. The resturaunt downstairs was quite good value, the buffet was very good but again lacking in much class, but the wine was good.The entertainment consited of a bass player and a girl standing under a tacky disco ball singing karoke, she wasnt a bad singer but niether a good one. I feel that the Hotel is not what I expected but the staff try really hard to make up for the obvious problems.

<Author>miami93
<Content>Riu Florida Beach Hotel Having read several reviews before we left we were slightly prepared for the worse but this was not the case. Firstly every staff member that we met, be it the front desk, the bar staff, pool staff, waitresses, conceirge were extremely polite and helpful. Our room was clean and of a good size with everything that we needed and beds and towels changed daily. The pool area was lovely, spacious and clean with plenty of sun beds. Breakfast was excellent, loads of fresh fruit, fresh bread, meats, salads, bacon, sausages, eggs etc etc. The evening buffet was OK but quite frankly with the number of restaurants in Miami we did not eat there except on the first night. The beach was opposite the hotel only separated by a beautiful board walk. The beach was clean and beds and umbrellas were available at a charge or we just took our towels down and enjoyed the sun and sea. On this trip it was just my husband and I who went and it was perfect. I think teenagers would be a little bored as, apart from shopping there is not much to do until they are old enough for the clubs. Small children were well serviced by the pool and beach and taxis waited outside the hotel all day. Whether the Riu staff have taken note of some of the bad reports or whether some people had a bad experience I do not know but I can certainly say that for a week or more (if you want to go down to the Keys or Orlando) we both felt this hotel was an excellent choice.

<Author>Cazanne12
<Content>Sub-standard service  I stayed with my family at the Riu Hotel during February 2008. The grading for this hotel was extremely over exaggerated. We've stayed at better 2 and 3 star hotels in Miami in the past where the service/customer care was within that hotel grading. The service and customer care was very sub-standard and almost non-existent. There was a constant lack of bath towels, hand towels, face flannels, toiletries were left in our room by housekeeping on a regular basis. Several complaints about the lack of essential amenities for our room (3 times daily the first time it occurred then twice daily thereafter) via the front desk to no avail throughout the course of our two week holiday. Spare toilet tissue and face tissues were not made available to us - we complained a few times about these issue too. We had read the negative reviews about this hotel prior to our arrival in Miami on trip advisor and informed our package holiday provider to move us to another hotel prior our arrival but no spaces were available elsewhere due to the Boat Show. We therefore gave this hotel the benefit of the doubt - what a bad move that was! The bar food was sub-standard and cold. The bar entertainment/singer was sub-standard and sang songs completely out of her ability/capability! We left several messages for our local travel rep to make contact with us so we could convey our various complaints on negative issues to no avail - the rep was non-existent. The front desk didn't provide the customer care you would expect in accordance with the hotel grading - all they did was to write our room number on the corner of the desk pad but either ignored our requests or plainly forgot! (understandable if the are not writing proper details down). The housekeeping staff didn't speak/converse in English which is strange working in an American hotel where the main language spoken is English/American. Only one lift was operational at the hotel for nearly the entire duration of our holiday! The poorly maintained emergency staircase was the only other means to get to rooms on higher floors if you didn't want to wait at least 10 minutes for the one workable lift - we were based on the 6th floor with two under 6's! Guests were using the emergency staircase to checkout with their heavy luggage - very much a health and safety issue. On the last morning at breakfast black bits were found at the bottom of two glasses of apple juice obtained from the machines for my children - I wasn't impressed! Definitely not a 3.5 star hotel! Some of the food was overcooked, dry or re-heated food from previous day. The first room we were allocated on the 8th floor smelled musky and damp so we had to prolong our check-in and admin it entailed by request another room at front desk - the Riu hotel were already made aware of various negative issues read by me on trip advisor and conveyed to our local rep in the UK before our departure. Needless to say I have written a very strong letter of complaint to our holiday package provider on the negative aspects and our experience at the Riu!!!

<Author>rsekeres
<Content>Great Pool, OK Rooms We stayed at the Riu Florida Beach hotel while attending the nearby Yacht Show. We were prepared for the worst, based on other reviews, but were pleasantly surprised by the reasonably good experience.Positives: Beautiful pool area with easy access to the beach. Friendly valets and maid service, with OK front desk staff. Good location for visiting the yacht show (Walking distance). Food/wine prices were surprisingly modest for a hot vacation destination.Negatives: Room was passable, but sheets were coarse, carpet was matted, and there was no iron or ironing board (but there was a holder where one might've been). The restaurant sufficed for one meal, but it lacks atmosphere.There's definitely a European feeling to the way the hotel's managed. They call themselves a 4-star, but there's no way. Priceline gives them 3 stars, which is accurate.Overall, it's a good bet for a budget-conscious traveler (relatively speaking, for this expensive area), who wants the location, but I wouldn't make it a destination in and of itself to enjoy.

South Beach is straight out the back of the hotel with Carlos' Hut supplying loungers, a bar, umbrellas, all at a price..but what a great location. I spent everyday on South Beach watching the posers and loving it. In the evening its a nice walk up the boardwalk to go out for dinner and get into the nightlife. For the ladies like myself though, if you're out clubbing, get a cab, those heels won't make the 15-20 minute walk from the nightlife. To see the Art Deco its about a 20 minute walk in the day and really nice. The hotel is well kept and the buffet breakfast is fabulous, no matter how hung over i always made it down for breakfast!! all in all a good hotel.

<Author>Budge_8
<Content>"Don't believe all you read!' If you read some of the reviews on this hotel you might have second thoughts about staying, but please don't be put off by the negative comments as this hotel is great and excellent value for money!We stayed at the Riu Florida Beach from 06 - 16 February 2008 (this was our second visit in just over one year to the hotel) and we could not fault a thing. The rooms have been recently refurbished and ours was clean and spacious. The breakfast was great with plenty of choice including fresh fruit, cereals, pastries and a selection of cooked items (bacon, eggs, sausages etc.) should you want them.The pool and garden areas were always clean and tidy and there are plently of sunbeds to relax on and soak up the sun. The pool itself is a good size and great for cooling yourself off, but I am not 100%sure whether it is heated - this is not a real issue if the temperature outside is in the high 70's or low 80's.From reading previous reviews you might think that some of the staff are rude, but during our stay we never came across anyone working at the hotel who was not courteous and polite. In fact all the staff (from reception, housekeeping, the waiters and the pool attendant) were very friendly indeed.OK, one of the lifts was out of action for most of our stay, but this did not really cause us any inconvenience even though our room was on the 9th floor - we just used the stairs. It was a good way to work off the breakfast in the morning. I understand if you are old, infirm or have young children this might cause difficulties, but most people are just lazy and given the option of walking or using a lift they would choose the lift all the time.The location of the hotel in my opinion is also great. It is not in the middle of the action, but close enough should you want to sample the famous Miami nightlife. Ocean Drive is a pleasant 40 minutes stroll away along the boardwalk and Lincoln Avenue approximately 30 minues. You can of course always use your car or take a taxi, but what is the point as you can hardly soak up the atmosphere by sitting is a air-conditioned box! The beach where the hotel is situated is wide, the sand is clean and unlike parts of the beach towards Ocean Drive it is not crowded. Having said that, the beach as a whole is excellent and great for walking on.Overall, I would recommend anyone to stay at the Riu Florida Beach Hotel. It might not be in everyones opinion Four Star, but I have certainly stayed in Five Star hotels around the world which do not come anywhere near the standard of accommodation and service offered by the Riu.

<Content>Much better than most reviews portrayed Having read the multiple reviews, I was somewhat concerned about what awaited us at this hotel. Firstly, yes, there is still only one lift working and if you have luggage then it is frustrating getting it up or down. But at other times, why not just take the stairs, particularly on the lower floors. We were on the 8th floor and frequently took the stairs. A bit of exercise is good for everyone afterall!I agree that the beds were not big enough for two people to share and the other gripe was not a hotel specific one but there did seem to be a number of Hispanic kids running the corridors at all hours. On the positive side, our room was lovely and our friends' room even bigger. The air conditioning was excellent and the beds were comfortable.The staff at reception I found extremely helpful and courteous and the breakfast was expansive and far better than other 4* hotels that we have stayed in, particularly the fruit and bread. Additionally, eating breakfast on the terrace looking over the lovely pool area was a great way to start each day.I will admit that you are a bit stuck for food choices if you don't have a car and agree with the previous reviewer who said to head for Tony Roma's. We did have a car and so didn't eat in the hotel other than breakfast so i can't comment on that.To the person who complained about no ESPN, I agree that I was surprised although it was nice to have 3 soccer channels for those of us that don't like to have our sport constantly punctuated by time outs every few minutes.If you have already booked to stay here and are worried about how you will experience the hotel, I would say not to be. There may be a few minor glitches but overall based on our experience, it was a really nice 4 days that we spent in the Riu

<Author>TorontoMinded
<Content>Don't believe all the bad reviews, but don't believe Riu's 4 stars either My wife and I booked a room at a good rate at this property over the Christmas Holidays 2007. We were spooked by all the bad reviews, particularly because RECENT reviews are particulary consistent in their negative comments, but since our travel plans were extremely last-minute we booked an available OceanFront room here anyway.Despite its four-star claims, this property is clearly no more than a THREE star property- clean and in a decent location (see below), but with some real problems. Those prepared to put up with a few inconveniences won't mind their stay here. Those seeking a four star experience, or expecting a similar level of care or quality as you would find at other Riu properties should DEFINITELY look elsewhere.LOCATION: For us, perfect. A 20 minute walk down Collins Ave or the boardwalk along the beach. This is a quieter stretch of the main beach/hotel street. This was perfect for us, as the beach up at 31st is as beautiful as it is along Ocean Drive, and we appreciated the quietness. If you are headed to Miami Beach primarily for the clubs or the party (plenty of that to find here), I would recommend a Hotel along Collins or Ocean Drive, but at 15th street or Lower. (Addresses along Collins are easy, as they correspond to the numbered cross street closest to where you are staying. Our hotel was at 3101, so you know right away it's at Collins and 31st. The busy stretch of Miami Beach runs from 7th to 15th.) I personally would not recommend a hotel much farther north than the 30's if you are planning on walking the city.THE ROOM: We stayed on the fifth floor in an oceanview room. Nicely renovated, new furnishings in good condition. Other reviews have mentioned a bad smell. We noticed nothing but a standard hotel aroma. Room was clean, except for the beasties mentioned below.The Hotel is an L shape, and half of the so-called Ocean View rooms- those that run along the leg of the L that is perpendicular to the beach, would be better described as partial ocean view. I doubt that any rooms on floors lower than ours could see the ocean at all. Still, the pool area is lovely, green and gardened, with palm trees and a few slivers of ocean horizon peeking through, and the ocean side rooms have good size terraces that are clean and bright. No complaints, just don't expect the surf rolling right outside your window or anything like that.THERE IS STILL ONLY ONE ELEVATOR WORKING. BE PREPARED TO USE THE STAIRS OR WAIT AND WAIT AND WAIT.THE COCKROACHES: We killed FIVE in a three day stay. Not sure this is avoidable, but it always taints one's opinion of the room, yes?THE POOL: In small print in one information folder tucked in your drawer, you are warned that the pool is hyper-chlorinated every evening for cleaning, and is unsafe for use. We were told variously that this dangerous treatment happens at 6, 7:30, 8, 10 and never. Two problems with this: one, hard to feel cared for in a hotel that shuts its pool down before the sun is down (we would have enjoyed an evening swim) and TWO...THE STAFF: Believe the surplus of negative reviews on this subject... the staff at the Riu Miami Beach don't know anything about the pool, the area, the restaurant, their own hotel, and they clearly don't care to find out. This is the single-most irritating characteristic of this property. Not well-managed, and you certainly won't feel taken-care-of, much less pampered here. I can't imagine staying at this hotel for more than a single day without experiencing some frustration or annoyance at the staff here.In short, I would only recommend staying at this property if you get a very good deal and are fairly easy-going and easily-pleased. This Riu is certainly not worth a 4star price, although with a little patience for its flaws, we found it an enjoyable and reliable home-base for a quick trip to Miami Beach.  
<Date>Dec 31, 2007

<Content>Great Beach We booked a 3 nites stay at the Riu after our Bahamas cruise. We wanted a place near the beach and also near South beach. We paid $180/nite. <Author>svvt
<Content>Don't use the telephones to call home We arrived at the hotel at 4pm to find a short que. We were soon seen to by a very helpful lady called beau and ask for a room with a sea view and were given this for 20 dollars a night, a discount of 10 dollars per night on the usual price. Our room while small was lovely, it was on the top floor which I was also pleased about. The room had 2 double beds, not the most comfy but not the worse I have slept on. The air con was fantastic as was having a fridge in the room. Also the hair-dyer was brilliant by hotel standards. The pool area was very pretty however very very very busy, hense we never in our 2 week holiday took a dip. The beach was lovely regardless of what other people have said on this site its like being within a postcard. While it may have a little sea-weed in it (but what do people expect its the sea after all) it was lovely and warm and very blue. We ate dinner in the hotel on various occasions while not brilliant it was cheep enough. The lifts within the hotel were terrible. The staff used the same lifts for moving various bits of bedding about and god knows what. On more than 10 occasions there was only 1 lift working and myself and my partner had to walk the 10 floors to our room. Staffs attitudes were indifferent if not difficult on most occasions. You would be speaking to a member of staff about a subject then the member of staff would break of conversation and begin to have another additional conversation with thier colleague in another language, quite rude. We used the hotel phones every other day to ring home for no longer than 2 minutes at a time, DO NOT DO THIS!! upon checking out from the hotel we were landed with a bill of over 600 dollars yeah thats right 600 dollars. Now while monies not a real issue with me, being ripped off is. I didn't expect the telepgone bill to be cheep but not 600 plus dollars. I spoke to the manager and while she was understanding of the sitution and informed me that hotel phones are always expensive and I should have used an external pay phone, I paid in full. Note however that nowhere in the hotel is there a list of costs relating to telephone calls. Miami is awesome, don't eat on ocean drive AS ITS SOOO expensive and the food isnt that great, however do get a drink and people watch. Esponola way is brilliant, theres an awesome bar, as it B.E.D on washington the most amazing food. Thalula just off collins (not far from the hotel) is also awesome, the food is out of this world. We also ate at a chinesse on washington and that was brilliant too. We spent about 150 dollars on average on a 3 course meal with lots of drinks for two, good value. Oh and another tip we got take out twice to our room and on both occasions it was horrible, I can't remember what the first place was called but the second was called the big pink cafe and tasted like yuk! Also make sure if you are going to Miami you get a guide book we got two and they were invaluble. Also go to KEYWEST, its awesome, the other keys do not even come close. Stay at the southernmost on the beach and eat at lattitudes on sunset key, very very romantic and lovely. All in all amazing holiday and will be back to miami just not the riu and will definatley be back to keywest and the southernmost on the beach. PS - HIRE A CAR ITS A MUST!!!

<Author>rawaspecial
<Content>We expected something better We just returned from a holiday in Florida with one of the hotels being the RIU Florida Beach. After staying 6 nights at the Crowne Plaza Orlando Universal (which I can highly recommend!) and spending much less on the hotel room there we expected something alike as they also both have 4 stars. Boy, were we wrong! First impression: grand Lobby but shabby. Upon arrival we also discovered there was a 14 USD fee for valet parking. Check-in was smooth and quick since we had prepaid hotel vouchers. We asked for a room with ocean or partial ocean view and were told that this was not possible due to our rate!The elevators were absolutely past their times - extremely old and grimy  dirty carpets inside!!! When we left they had just begun to renovate them. But in my opinion they should also add at least one more elevator, as the hotel is quite big. We were given room 920 which is right across from the elevator on the 9th floor. It was a very big room with two beds but that was the only thing positive about it. It did not have the look of a four star hotel nor the look of having been renovated recently either - worn furniture and a shabby carpet. The window looked out unto the main street with an ugly, half torn down building across. The bathroom was quite small compared to the size of the room and it was made even smaller by the fact that the door to the bathroom could not be opened fully as it pushed against the sink!!! We have never seen anything like it!!! We complained  checked with the front desk and were then given a nicer room - 923, which also had partial ocean view. Then we went to the pool  beach. Pool area is very nice with enough beds, tables, chairs etc. The beach  sea were quite nice too - sometimes the water was a little dirty though with algae and trash swimming around, but I guess thats normal for a huge city like Miami. We slept quite well as beds are big and comfy but during next morning we were awakened by the elevator bells chimes we heard even from far around the corner! I cannot imagine what it would have been like in room 920!!! Later we went for the buffet breakfast, which was included in our stay and everyone else's too as the place was packed and very noisy! Breakfast included the usual fruit (4 kind), jams  spreads, toast  bread, cold cuts, cheese, french toast, pancakes, omeletts etc. A nice variety of almost everything and staff very courteous and fast setting up the tables. Luckily we went to the pool area not too late as all the nice, shaded areas were quickly taken, especially by people getting up early and leaving their towels there only to return much later - the old european towel trick. At lunch my kid ordered a hamburger with fries (9,92 USD) and a small (cordial) juice (8,68!!!). Never again as the fries tasted old and were not even hot and the juice was much too expensive! We never had any other food there except the included breakfast. Re the insects mentioned in previous reviews: I did find one or two ants in our room, but since it had a fridge this did not pose a problem. My husband  I did see one (live) cockroach in the buffet area during breakfast though, but in a hot climate this can be very common, and I am not squeamish. Would probably have caused a big fuss if I had shouted out loud that there is a cockroach... Needless to say, the negative facts outweigh the positive facts and I would not stay at the hotel ever again. We were very disappointed.

<Author>SummerSR
<Content>Very happy with our stay... First let me say I have taken many vacations and this is the first time I've ever written a review. I felt compelled to do so because of all the outdated and/or horrible reviews the RIU has gotten.My family (me, my husband and 2 daughters ages 21  9) stayed in room804 (oceanfront) for 7 days at Easter time. The hotel was completely booked. We booked through a travel agency and got a great rate. I wasa little nervous because of the low rate....then reading some of the reviews I almost tried to cancel. Good thing I didn't because we had a great time. The hotel has 10 floors and 10 through 7 had been renovated at the time we were there. They said by June the whole hotel would be done. Not sure if it looked like that would happen. I heard someone say 4 was the only floor they allowed smoking. OK let's see...our room (804) was obviously just renovated....everything...carpet..bedding.. ceiling fan...furniture...drapes..bathroom...balcony tiles...were all brand new. We had 2 full sized beds..plenty of drawer space...large mirrored closet and a small table with 2 chairs. There was NO smell...no mildew and I neversaw a bug inside the property the whole time we were there. There wasa small fridge..basic hotel blow dryer...iron and ironing board in the room. There is a safe you can rent in the room for $2 a day. The TV was fine...had HBO/cable....also movies you can rent....I don't remember the exact price but it was expensive.The maid was very nice and efficient. She brought us extra towels and extra pillows when we asked.Check-in went OK.....we got there early and they got us a room 3 hours before the 4pm check-in time. The elevators were really one of the only things that were bad. They were slow and not too clean because we had to share them with the workers that were doing the construction. Which by the way we never heard. Also no noise coming from other rooms.I would say out of everyone staying there we were one of the few Americans.....mostly European...a mix of families and couples young  old.On the hotel restaurant...had we known what we know now we would have definitely tried to get a breakfast plan. It looked like many guests had breakfast included in their stay. There really aren't any restaurants right around the hotel....which for dinner was fine because we wanted to go down to Lincoln Road/Ocean Drive most nights....but in the morning when you need coffee immediately the hotel restaurant was the only real choice. And it was pretty good. It's $12 pp adults...$6 kids. (plus tax and tip) Full buffet.....chef there making omelets with whatever fillings you choose...pancakes...french toast...bacon..sausage..eggs...potatoes...fresh fruit...cereals...muffins..danish..yogart..cottage cheese...all kinds of breads...juices and of course unlimited coffee.The hotel grounds were very nice. The pool was clean and a decent size for Miami beach standards. We walked the boardwalk and looked at many other hotels and the RIU pool/lounge area looked great in comparison. The sand/beach was a little dirty.......just like most of the other beach areas we looked at from the south end on up. The water itself was VERY nice...clean and clear. One morning it was a little cloudy but we had bad thunderstorms all night. My older daughter bought snorkeling gear in a little shop about 3 blocks south of the hotel on Collins Ave. Because of the rocks that were there the water is calmer for the kids and there were tons of colorful fish around the rocks....lots of people were snorkeling. We were sorry we didn't bring one of those disposable under water cameras.The cab from Miami International airport was $32 plus tip. From the hotel down to Lincoln Road the cab rides were approx. $7 plus tip. There was also a bus that stopped right outside the hotel. (not sure of the cost, we never took it) You could also walk the boardwalk and get to the heart of SoBe in about 20 minutes. If you are looking for a hotel right in the middle of everything in SoBe then this isn't for you. Or if you are looking for a luxurious hotel where the staff pampers you...forget it...lol...for the most part they were pretty aloof. It really depended upon who was helping you....some really went out of their way to be nice and helpful and some had a yeah whatever attitude. The pool area bar....the food there was OK....burgers, sandwiches  fries were decent. Frozen drinks were great. What was really good was on Friday, Saturday  Sunday they barbecue. The guy doing it was very nice. He made some sort of marinated steak and beef, chicken or shrimp kabobs that were delicious!We would definitely stay there again.

<Author>Sues-travels
<Content>Pleasantly Surprised I was really worried about this hotel after reading some of the terrible reviews but was only booked for 3 days and thought I would chance it. We arrived early to be greeted by a very pleasant guy (Dave) and lady on reception, it was our anniversary and they congratulated us. We had a room on the top renovated level and could not fault it. We ate breakfast on the terrace each morning and there was a good choice with lots of healthy options. The pool area was excellent, nicely laid out with plants and trees and the loungers plentiful with beach towels provided daily. A few steps and you were on the beach. OK it was a walk to the main area but a very pleasant walk either on the beach or the boardwalk so no problem there either. All in all it was a lovely hotel - my son and his wife were staying at the Delano and paying mega money, we spent a day with them around their pool but to be honest I preferred ours. This was a surprising lovely start to a 16 day holiday throughout Florida.

<Content>Very disappointing....newly renovated means still working on it! Yes, the lobby is great, but is that where you will spend your time? This hotel is under renovation, they started at the top and are working their way down, so get an upper floor. I complained about the early morning construction next door so they moved me to a room right above the floor they were working on! The walls are paper thin, a normal conversation can be heard through the walls. The only saving grace was the pool area and the beach. They do have plenty of lounge chairs and towels available. I did not notice any trash on the beach as someone reported. This hotel is 20 blocks north of Lincoln road. A cab ride will cost $10. I have stayed in Miami several times and am disappointed that I didn't book the Four Points or Marriott instead. This was a travel partner's choice based on their Cancun visits to Riu properties. The unrenovated floors are very shabby, chairs in room were dirty and the carpet is filthy. The 2 elevators are slow. If you don't care about the room and distance from buzz of south beach, the pool and beach are great. Get a balconey room to make it more bearable! There's a little Cuban market that sells espresso and cheap breakfasts 2 blocks up the boardwalk...the hotel coffee is bad and expensive...take the walk to start your day! We did not eat in the restaurant and the pool-side service wasn't bad.

<Content>The Most Disgusting Hotel Ever! Stay Away First let me start off by saying that I am not a picky person when it comes to travel. As long as the room is clean, there is a place to lay out in the sun and there is a bar I'm good! That's all I ask for. Well, let me tell you- this is the dirtiest, most disgusting hotel I have ever stayed in! When we first arrived I thought hmmm the lobby is nice, there are palm trees all around, there is a bar, I'm gonna have a great vacation. Check in took literally 45 minutes!! And I was only second in line! So Ok no problem, no big deal...we finally get the room key and go to the elevator...1 was broken and the other one had 15 people waiting to get on....that one ended up being stuck between floors so we had to carry all our luggage up 4 flights of stairs sweating our butts off. NO BELL BOY! Ok no problem, I brushed that off. We got to our rooms and the smell smacked me in the face as soon as we open the door...dank musty, moldy, smokey rotten smell. I asked for another room, there were none so they say, so now we are stuck there. I opened up the door to the balcony and the curtains were brown with smoke residue!! Yuck. We go out on the balcony and notice that you can't even leave the door open or unlocked because your balcony litterally touches the persons balcony next to you, with only a 4 foot wall seperating it, so anyone could hop over it and get on your balcony and go in your room. Didn't like that, but whatever.So we got changed and headed to the pool. Dirty green disgusting small pool, like the size that would be in your backyard. So we said OK lets forget the pool and head to the beach. <Author>rettie
<Content>Stop Slagging the Riu We spent our honeymoon in 1980 in this hotel when it was called the Sans Souci, came back in 2005 for our Silver Wedding.Found the hotel had greatly improved over the years, loved the lobby and all the changes Riu had made to what had been a very dated but beautiful hotel. I too had read the mixed reviews but glad we took the plunge and stayed here.  The pool back in 1980, was very large with a diving board, no shade, just lots of loungers, just loved the thoughtful planning of the pool area and all the lovely shade available when the sun got too hot. If you were unlucky and hadn't grabbed a shady spot,  when the pool attendant thought you were beginning to look fried he attentively came over and put up an umbrella. Didn't find the towel thing a problem, this is how it works in most hotels I have stayed in in the States where towels are supplied.The staff were brilliant, very friendly and even gave us flowers  a cake on our anniversary. Breakfast was wonderful, sitting out on the verandah even on the edge of a hurricane, the staff did their best to keep the area open.Although I would have preferred a front room we had a side room with a view of the ocean, it was very clean and compared well with other hotels we have stayed in in Miami.Would certainly go backSure there isn't much in the area except other hotels but if you want the bright lights and bars of SoBe stay down there. We always rent a car in Miami and use valet parking so finding nice places to eat is never a problem. The only thing I missed in 2005 was not being able to go to Ma Flynn's Pub under the hotel next door, used to be a good safe haven away from the daily thungerstorms!As for the area looking a bit run down, if you want run down, look back at the early '80s and how bad SoBe was, It was a SCARY place back then.Having come to Miami for 27 yrs, I have found that each area goes in cycles, when the renovations in this area are done, it will look nice but this will then show up other areas and so the cycle continues.Sorry for the rant will be checking out the Riu myself this summer.

<Content>OK Hotel, Bad Location Not a bad hotel, good value, the rooms are quite a nice size and were clean. Nice big windows, so the rooms were lovely and light. It was free which is the most positive thing you can say about it!!!Lovely location right on the beach. That is the only good thing about the location though. Don't believe what the Virgin brochure says about lots of restaurats within walking distance - the only restaurants within walking distance are in other hotels - there is literally nothing else! South Beach is about a 25 minute walk in one direction, but that is a long way to walk at night, especially with a full belly, and very limited parking if you drive there. i would recommend that if you want to eat drive to (its too far to walk) Sunny Isles where there were endless restarants. Actually - i would just stay in Sunny Isles, there were plenty of nice looking hotels!! If you just want to lay on the beach and eat in the hotel then you will be fine here.

<Content>Very Enjoyable I stayed at this hotel with my partner and we both found the stay very pleasant. The lobby is quite big and open, as with other guests we too had long waiting times for the lifts but some people were very unreasonable about it, shouting at staff if they had to wait more than 30 seconds! The rooms are spacious and our room had 2 large beds. The choice of TV channels was good, the balcony was huge and we had a magnificent sea view.On one particular day we decided to have a lie-in and forgot to put the 'do not disturb' sign on the door, the cleaner did not knock, she just walked in, she did try her best to apologise in broken english though.We found the staff at the hotel to be extremely friendly and helpful, willing to give us info on where to go and where to stay away from. One member of staff gave us a take away menu so that we could order food to our hotel room after the restaurant closed as there wasn't anywhere else to get food nearby. I would definately stay in this hotel again.

<Author>awesommmmmeee
<Content>SuperBowl Disaster! A large group of my coworkers and I arranged to stay here during the 2007 SuperBowl. First off, the lobby is pretty nice, but everything else is pretty much dated and has an odd smell. If you're looking for up-to-date amenities, I suggest you look elsewhere. Secondly, there's no internet in any of the guest rooms. There's wireless in the lobby, but this poses a problem when taking work-related calls in the lobby of a busy hotel. Not very professional background noise! The pool area is ok, but the towels they give out are old and rough, and there is no hot tub/jacuzzi. There's a hotel bar, but it closes at midnight, which makes for a hard time to go out, considering the next closest bar is at least an 11 block walk, since you're so far off from everything. As far as meal options are concerned, the hotel offers breakfast, but I wouldn't be able to tell you how it is, considering the reastaurant literally closes at 10 am, and does not reopen until dinner, at 6:30 pm. For those of you who like to sleep in after a late night, good luck getting food. There's a bodega about three blocks away, and your only other meal option within 10 blocks is a mediocre Italian restaurant 5 blocks away. Literally, that's about all there is in the area. During my 6 night stay, I spent a total of $180 on cabs, just going to the beach and restaurants. Luckily, I can expense these charges, but if you're on vacation, these are coming out of your pocket. I reccommend staying elsewhere that might be a little more expensive, but at least you'll be saving yourself the hassle of having to catch a cab anytime you want to do anything.The view also left much to be desired, considering it was a very large view of an impressive concrete wall and pillar. A coworker two doors down had a better view-about half of the window, if he leaned forward, was of the water. Unfortunately, I wasn't so lucky. Finally, the elevators are an issue, too. There's only two for a 10-story hotel, so you spend quite a lot of time waiting. There are no clearly marked stairways, so even if you only want to go one flight up or down, you have to wait for an elevator. Wear comfortable shoes.Last time I was here, I stayed at a cute boutique place on Ocean Drive for actually $10 less per night, and it was far superior. Definitely keep looking if you'd like to enjoy your vacation-this hotel is not where you want to go!Side note: The staff, while mostly native Spanish-speakers, were actually very helpful and pleasant. Unfortunately, they do not make up for a poorly-thought out hotel.

<Author>Nibbles
<Content>Fantastic staff - Great for a few nights We stayed here for a couple of nights , 1 pre and one post-cruise. The hotel is dated, as some guests have stated, this is particularly evident in the bedrooms eg single-glazed windows, doors showing some wear and tear and the location isn't ideal to be right on top of the actionHowever, the rooms were large and clean and adequately furnished and it's right on the beach with a man-made breakwater providing an ideal swimming area. The public rooms and pool area are all kept in excellent condition and the breakfast buffet was particularly good (and included in the price). The free WiFi in the lobby was a useful extra for those with their own laptops.Our pre-night cruise was spent in a room on the side with single-glazed window which meant that noise from the street was evident and I would think that those rooms facing onto Collins may have a problem. For our post-cruise night we requested a beach front room with balcony and were lucky to get a corner room with windows on 2 walls and a very spacious balcony (at no extra cost).The boardwalk between the hotel and the beach provided a nice stroll down to Lincoln (where we found lots of bars and restaurants) - around 20 mins walk. Whilst the area around the hotel is a little run down, many of the hotels around the area are currently undergoing refurb and within a year or two I expect the area will be very stylish, much like the area further south.What particularly struck me about this place was the friendliness of the staff - without exception every one of them provided excellent, caring service. Interestingly enough, most of the clientele seemed to be European, perhaps because the hotel is owned by a European company.I would definitely stay here again if I could guarantee a beach-view room.

<Author>jewelsoftravel
<Content>would stay again We stayed at this hotel September 2-5, 2006. I found it to be a nice upper-moderate hotel. It definitely has an international feel....the staff are from all over the world. Nice big marble lobby, which the staff constantly keeps clean. Valet is about your only option for parking, unless you snag a street spot - don't hold your breath. We were fortunate to get an oceanfront room with balcony. The room was what you'd expect from a moderate. The beds were quite hard (like you'd find in Mexico). My only complaint here was that the dresser drawers had a very powerful musty/old smell to them, so I just didn't use it. They use the old style safes, where they give you the lock/key. Be sure not to over-pack the safe or the lock will stick. We were very pleased with the location and the beach. We were relatively close to South Beach. We only had breakfast at the hotel one morning, but I was totally satisfied with the choices. They had an omelet station, egg - any way you want, among other options. We never stuck around in the evening, but we did notice that they had some sort of entertainment most nights. They offer internet services for a fee, but luckily you purchase how much you want - and can log in and out at will until used up. All in all, we were pleased with our stay. Yeah, maybe the decor could be updated, but you come to Florida to see the sights - not your room.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>there's nothing wrong with this hotel! we've just returned from our honeymoon, and the riu florida beach was the last destination on our trip which also included vegas and mexico. Yeah, this hotel wasnt as good as the hotels we stayed in in those places, but it was still absolutely fine. i dont think the people writing all the bad reviews on this site bothered to check it out before hand. either that or they just like to moan. the hotel has a nice big lobby, and the rooms are perfectly ok. maybe could do with a bit of redecoration but not because they are dirty, just a bit dated. the pool area is lovely, as it the pool bar. The breakfast buffet is everything you could ask for and more, and the hotel staff were nothing but nice to us, giving us directions, telling us about which tours to do, and letting us use another room to shower in after we had checked out of our room on our last day, for free. i've stayed in plenty of hotels where they have made you pay for this. there are obviously beeter hotels to stay in in miami, but not for this price. there is a boadwalk at the back of the hotel (which is right on the beach) where you can walk all the way down to south beach. this takes about 40 minutes, but with gorgeous beach and sea views all the way, whats the hurry?! Ocean drive and the art deco district are not to be missed, especially at night. Lincoln road is also worth a visit, about 25-30mins walk from the hotel, its a nice pedestrainised street with shops and loads of places to eat. On the whole Miami is a great city, and this hotel has everything you need. we'll definatley be back.

<Author>mtnstreamdream
<Content>not my favorite place After reading many reviews my daughter and I made reservations at the RIU for our Miami vacation. I was disappointed. The beach was dirty, lined with trash and seawood. I would think the staff would clean up the beach every morning like they do at other places I've stayed. It only takes a few minutes, but makes a world of difference. The walls were so thin, if anyone is staying in rooms on either side, you can hear every sound they make. One morning the neighbor had checked out but left their 6 am alarm on. It rang for 15 minutes before anyone came up after a call to the desk to shut it off. Mostly I was upset because they don't have a coffee maker in the room, or any complimentary cups. I had to go to the bar in the evenings for a small china cup of $2.15 coffee, and the dining room in the mornings. The buffets at the hotel are expensive and there aren't any clean places to eat within walking distance. The balcony isn't private at all. If you sit on your balcony, you can see the people on each side of you and clearly hear the conversations. Valet parking is $12 a day. I'd prefer to park my own car anyway, but wasn't given that option. I won't go back, although Miami is a beautiful city and has lots of interesting things to do, I just had to stay away from the hotel as much as possible! Oh, the people played in the pool all night, and once again, with the thin walls, that's all you could hear...no calming ocean waves.

<Author>Speukes
<Content>How did this become a 4 star hotel? We stayed 4 nights at this hotel, and we regret it. It's just not worth the money.Our room had no balcony, and we missed that a lot. It was comparable with a motel room: stains in the bath, dirty windows that we couldn't get opened, no fridge, ... The image of our TV was often disturbed, caused by a bad cable. It reported this at the reception. When we came back to our room, we noticed someone had looked at it, but nothing was replaced so our TV stayed unreliable for the next 4 days.The staff is (like the majority of Miami Beach) native Spanish speaking. They have problems speaking English, I have problems speaking English (and we don't know a single word Spanish), so communications were often difficult.Housekeeping was knocking on our door at 8.15 a.m.. Some people like to sleep when they're having a holiday.When we arrived with our rental car, we were almost forced to park it in the valet parking. I returned the car to the rental company half an hour later. At check-out, we received a 4 x $12 check for the 4 nights our car would had been in the valet parking... I explained our situation, and we were promised we wouldn't have to pay it (I'm curious...)Internet in the lobby is expensive and rather slow ($4 for 15 minutes, $7 for 30 minutes). There's a internet shop between 28th and 29th Street asking half of that price, with doubled speed. There's also a nice Cuban restaurant in that block.Ocean Drive and Lincoln Road Mall are an hour away if you choose to walk. You can take the bus to Lincoln Road, that bus stop is a few steps from the hotel. The bus to Aventura Mall stops right in front of the hotel. Sure, it's not all bad at this hotel: the swimming pool and pool bar are nice. And honestly: the breakfast-buffet was the best we ever had in a hotel. It was also the only hotel in our Florida-trip that gave something (champagne and fruit) because of our honeymoon.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>will never stay here again My boyfriend and I just returned from Miami last week. We stayed at this hotel for 4 nights and 5 days. I truly do not recommend this hotel for future vacationers. We arrived at the Riu on a Sunday morning. They luckily had a room for us ready when we got there. So we both carried our bags up to the 5th floor to find out that the room key/card didn't work. Come to find out, it wasn't the key, someone was already in that room. After inserting the card/key numerous times, the door majically opened to another person occupying the room. So we dragged our luggage back down to the main lobby where we waited for the front desk to find us another room. And you guessed it, they had another room. So again, my boyfriend and I dragged our luggage back up to now the 7th floor. Keep in mind, we paid for and requested an Oceanview and non-smoking room. Good news... the key worked. Bad news... it was a smoking room. And it wasn't an oceanview room. So I called down to the front desk and said that I requested a nonsmoking room and an oceanview room. They said that this was the only room they had available and that we should wait for a couple hours to see what comes available. So we waited a couple of hours and I called inbetween to check, while getting transfered to numerous people whom didn't have any idea who I was or what was going on. Finally, a knock on the door! A gentleman from the front desk coming to take us and our luggage to yet another room. This room was nice and was nonsmoking and had an oceanview. So after 1/2 of our day was wasted we ventured out to get something to eat. (The hotel does not have room service either.) Eating there is another experience. They only offer breakfast and dinner. Breakfast is served for 2.5 hours: from 7:30 until 10am. It is $12 a person and they charge 11% tax. Believe me, there are much nicer, better, cheaper places to eat breakfast in Miami. Dinner is served for yet again only 2.5 hours: from 6:30 until 9pm. We didn't even consider eating there. The beach/pool. The pool was ok. Kinda dirty and the towels were very rough. Speaking of rough towels... bring your own! The towels in the rooms were horribly rough and small. The beach was nice, kinda dirty, and yet again they were charging more $ to rent chairs or an umbrella. We already paid to stay here and if you want to sit in a chair they charge you $6 per chair and $8 for an umbrella. And don't even think about renting a car unless you want to spend $12 a day for the hotel to park it for you. We had to rent a car, especially because the hotel is 15 blocks from everything. Luckily, we found free street parking because we weren't giving the hotel any more of our money. We will never stay there again. Don't let the pictures fool you. Its a dump.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Lovely hotel, showing it's age We stayed at the Riu between 9th May - 16th May. The hotel itself is lovely for a 3 star hotel. The hotel staff were just so wonderful - especially Ozbel, who must have an extra mention! We asked about upgrading our room to an ocean view on arrival as we couldnt book through our agent. This was no trouble at all, and he also arranged for a bottle of champagne  a fruit platter to be sent to our room as we were celebrating our 12th anniversary. Our room had a fantastic view of the beach and overlooked the pool area. The room itself could do with spruceing up, but again, this is a 3 star hotel, not the Ritz! The beds were a little too hard for us, and smaller than the average American double, we thought. There is no tea/coffee facilities which is a shame, as there is no room service and breakfast does not open till 7.30am sharp - not a minute before! There is a mini bar though! The area surrounding the hotel does seem to be a bit 'run down'. There could be some regeneration work going on, as there is an awful lot of buiding work going on (just next door, The Saxony seems to be in the process of being rebuilt) Although Google Earth shows a Dennys restaurant nearby, this is now closed. In fact, all the shops on that parade are closed with the possible exception of a moped shop - it was impossible to tell, as it looked closed, but there was a chained up moped in the window! However there is a small 'supermarket' (or corner shop / grocer shop) on the corner, just past the Saxony. Bar prices are as you would expect - hotel prices. I would have loved to have given this hotel 5 out of 5 but just a few points prevented that. However, as I've said, for a 3* hotel, you really cant go wrong as long as you expect 3*!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great and beautifull stay Stayed in the Riu Florida Beach for two weeks (8-20) with my girlfriend and just loved it. We had a room on the 9th floor (910) non-smoking with an oceanview. Despite some of the bad reviews of this hotel we went for it and didn't experience any of the problems from the past reviews. Here are our + and - points we experienced during our stay in RFB.+ POINTS- The food was great and normal priced- Excellent pool with service (sometimes hard to find a place in busy times) - Friendly staff (and they all do speak english)- Spacious and clean room, a lot of fun channels on the tv, good shower beam, excellent  oceanview- Good cleaning of the rooms- Two busstops in front of the hotel (1.50 pp all the way) (5 min lincon road 8 min ocean  drive)- Supermarkt (small) nearby - Super easy acces to the beach (which isn't busy)- POINTS- Drinks were a bit overpriced but ok (get you're drinks out the vending machine)- Elevators are slow and to few elevators on busy times- The direct surrounding of the hotel is a bit abbanded (especcialy at night), all the fun is  just a few min away with the busTIPS- Always take a oceanview or aoceanfront room it is well worth the extra money. We have seen a normal room it that was pretty at all, not just the view but also the room itself- If you are a non-smoker always take a non-smoking room, the smell on the floors with smoking rooms is just awful.- When you have to check -out (12:00) at have to wait a lot of hours for you plain to leave, ask for the complemtary shower room. Then you can still swim some hours and take a quick shower before you're picked up for the airport.- Sign up for the free Riu-card [-] and you might get a beter service if you hand it over if you check in (and a free fruit basket).

<Author>Angel57
<Content>Great stay My family and I stayed here for 3 nights on arriving in Florida. We found the hotel to be clean and comfortable and we even had a partial view of the sea. The staff were very friendly and helpful. The breakfast was really good and set us up for the day. We walked to South Beach each day along the Boardwalk and walked back in the evening along the street. Although there were a few seedy areas along the walk back we never felt unsafe or threatened. We did the Duck Tour which was fun, however they did not cover the whole route as indicated on their leaflet, and most of the time was spent on the water looking at celebrity homes. If you are from the UK like us, most of them won't mean much to you. It is a fun trip though.The best place we ate was Joe Allen's. It was a little off the beaten track (junction of Dade Boulevard and Purdy Ave) but the food, service and atmosphere were great!Arranged to pick our Dollar hire car up from the Eden Roc hotel for 9.00am, we eventually got it at 11.00am! It didn't matter to us as we weren't in a hurry but there were a lot of frustrated people waiting there, so be warned.

<Author>MSkinner
<Content>Okay, but... Just got back from the RIU in South Beach, Miami. We stayed there for 2 days prior to our cruise (Mar 9  10th).The amenities were pretty good, and the rooms not bad. Not great, but not bad. I can only assume that they're still cleaning up from the past hurricane season, so I'll give them a little leeway.We had an ocean view room, 7th floor, and had a great view of the beach, ocean, and pool area. The beds were hard as a rock, as were the pillows (the pillows were about 2 inches thick - no cushion). Staff were generally friendly, but spoke very little English. We could barely understand the guy when we checked in, and all the forms we signed were in another language. And when you ordered a drink, for example, the bartender would acknowledge you  then start speaking in another language to his buddies behind the bar. They could be talking about the weather or about your wife - I don't know. But it's kind of rude. And yes, I know RIU is a European hotel chain, and most guests  employees speak spanish, but there should be at least SOME english there - it still is the USA's official language, is it not?The hotel isn't in the best section of South Beach - very few stores, no restaurants nearby, and a little rundown neighbourhood. But the touristy section is only a couple minute taxi ride away. And it is on the beach - a real beautiful section of beach and boardwalk, actually.Overall, not really worth the price. Definitely would not stay here again if I was in the Miami / South Beach area.

<Author>NYCTraveler60
<Content>A Mixed Bag at the Riu Florida Beach I stayed at the Riu for 6 nights in mid-February 2006 with my husband, 2 teenage sons and my parents. It was a mixed experience. We were very tired our first evening, and decided to eat dinner at the lobby bar. It took an hour and forty minutes for our food to arrive! Our waitress never explained the long wait and never apologized (maybe because, as in most Miami restaurants, the tip is included in the bill). My parents were given a peculiar room near the elevator that was half the size of the other rooms in the hotel. The television did not work. When they asked to be transferred, they were told that there were no other rooms available at the hotel for the next several days. They continued to ask every day, and were finally moved to a lovely, oceanview room with a balcony on the 4th night. There was no extra charge for the new room. I agree with earlier reviewers that the location is not ideal. There are very few restaurants within walking distance, although we did enjoy the Cuban restaurant 2 blocks south and the Italian restaurant in the Marriott, which is about 7 blocks north. We arrived just after a cold spell, and the unheated pool was really too cold to swim in for the first several days of our stay. It finally heated up to a reasonable temperature toward the end of our stay.

<Content>Wonderful Hotel Stayed at this hotel March 2-7 2006. Upon checking in we were very early arriving around noon. Check in is not until 3pm. We were not even expecting to get in, but one of the girls at the front desk said that our room was ready. The staff was very friendly and the hotel is older, but beautiful. There were 4, 25 yr old girls who stayed in the room and getting ready wasn't even horrible. We never ran out of hot water and there was enough room everywhere for 4 girls things! We had an ocean view room which is way worth to get. The balcony overlooks the pool and the beach. It's breathtaking! The pool is very nice and there are many chairs around. You need to get out there pretty early to get one. There are chairs available on the beach also. For this hotel the price is cheap and it is worth every penny. The food is ok, basic hotel food. They have food at the pool bar sandwiches and salads and then for dinner there is a buffet. There are many good restaurants around and in short distance. Everything is within walking distance or a 10 min cab drive almost anywhere in South Beach. Best restaurant China Grille on Washington Ave. Best meal I have ever had! Had a wonderful stay at the Riu and will definitely be back!!!!

<Content>Below standard even for at a discounted price Arrived early February with spouse and two children ages 10 and 11.Check in was disappointing as extra fees were charged to us on the spot for bringing along our two children at the last minute. <Author>ChernMan
<Content>Good price for Miami Beach, but not a great hotel My wife and I just returned from a two night stay at the Riu. As far as Miami Beach goes, the price was reasonable. It's not in the best area, but it's not too far from South Beach - walked there and back a couple of times. The breakfast buffet was plentiful, but not great (had better breakfasts at Dennys). The views are nice (we had an oceanview room) and the pool area was good, but there are definitely some deficiencies. First, the hotel only has rooms with two double beds - no queens, no kings. Perhaps our room was an anomaly, but I don't think I've slept in a more uncomfortable bed. Rock hard and pillows so flat, two of them stacked were still smaller than a typical hotel pillow. Third, the walls are paper thin. We had a very poor sleep both nights because we could hear the people in the rooms next to us and above us, every time a door opened anywhere on the floor and the elevators (even though we were about five rooms down from the elevator alcove). Overall, a moderately attractive outside package with sub-Motel 6 inside comfort. We definitely wouldn't go back.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Awesome Service even during a hurricane My family just returned from Miami where we were stranded during Hurricane Wilma. I can't say enough good things about the hotel and its staff. There was a hotel full of people, all of us nervous and afraid. The staff was more than wonderful. They made sure everyone had the breakfast buffet during the hurricane itself (the buffet that is wonderful under normal circumstances and was still wonderful without power) as well as packing a sack lunch for all of the hotel guests, including a sandwich, fruit and bottled water...free of charge. The staff was more than helpful for all of us who were stranded in Miami without flights home. They were courtous and upbeat and calming. We were more than impressed with the hotel when we first arrived under the best of conditiions and are in awe with the service under the worst of conditions.The hotel itself is very pretty with a wonderful pool area. The rooms are spacious, clean and very pretty. The housekeeping staff were wonderful, friendly and more than helpful. My only issue with the entire staff was the pool staff. He was frequently rude and inconsiderate. That aside, we couldn't have asked for a nicer hotel on the beach with an incredibly helpful staff!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>CAUTION!!!! THIEVES I took a vacation with my family on Aug 19 we check in at the RIU Hotel located at 3101 Coliins Ave. On August 22nd at 7:30pm I noticed that my wallet was missing from my bag in my hotel room. After searching the entire room to see if maybe it was misplaced I realized that indeed the wallet was stolen from the room. I reported this immediately to the hotel manager. She informed me that she could not do anything about this matter until the morning crew arrived the following day. She also said that she would call the police and report the incident. The following morning I was called to the general manager's office to discuss what steps would be taken to investigate my stolen purse. She proceeded to run the key pad to my room door through their computer system. This would show all entrances that were made to the room at a specific time. The computer system showed that a service employee entered the room at 4:50 pm earlier that that day. She also noted that this was not a schedule cleaning visit. This was also 10 minutes before my mom came back to our room. I then asked the manager to call the police so that I can report this matter. This was only at my request. The police came and took my report of what happened. Ten minutes after the police left which was 20 minutes before we were leaving to come back to New York, the manager and 2 employees showed up in the lobby where my family and I were seated. The manager had my wallet in her hand, saying that they found the wallet behind a magazine rack in the room. What a coincidence!!! I think not!!!. How is it possible that my wallet mysteriously showed up right before I was leaving? I checked my wallet and all my credit cards and my daughter's diamond earrings were present, however my $200 US dollars was gone. I was so disgusted by this whole incident. I never thought that something like this would happen to me. I know you should be aware of your surroundings and belongings when staying at a hotel, but you also stay at these hotels with the expectation of being safe and secure. It just goes to show that you CANNOT TRUST ANYONE.!Protect yourself at all times. DO NOT LEAVE YOUR MONEY, JEWELERY, PERSONAL DOCUMENTS OUT IN THE OPEN WHEN STAYING AT HOTELS. SincerelyLESSON WELL LEARNT!

<Author>notalamb
<Content>This is a good hotel - don't believe the knockers I agree with reviewer who said that anyone who had a problem with this hotel, has a problem themselves. The rooms were clean, and the service was fine. It is very Spanish speaking, it is Spanish owned but all of Miami is as well.The hotel reception is a beautiful area. They looked after the fabulous pool very well. Usual scrabble for beds in the morning, especially as there are a lot of people from the new Pope's country. The beach was in front, simply walk out of the pool area onto the boardwalk and the very clean beach is there. Only downside was that there were few restaurants within walking distance, but with the taxi fare to Art Deco district or Lincoln Road Mall being $6, who cares. This is no wild hotel, go to South Beach for that, and it isn't four star but you aren't paying $200 per night. If you are looking for a nice place in Miami Beach, this is it. This opinion is from a family of Brits who holiday around the world all the time. We know bad when we see it and this place really is OK. I gave it 5 stars to counterbalnce the absurd 1 stars other reviewers have unfairly given. I really rate it a 4 star on the Trip Advisor scale.If you want to know more feel free to e-mail me.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Don't listen to the bad reviews Our family of four stayed at the Riu the week after Easter, March 28 through April 3, 2005. After reading some of the reviews, I was pleasantly surprised. The hotel was very nice, friendly staff, large lobby, the room was clean, although a little cramped since all four of us were in one room. The pool and beach were beautiful. If you have a car you are only five minutes from the South Beach strip. One block from the hotel is a neat little food store/restaurant called Nehmer's (sp?) that has great coffee and pastries, breakfast, lunch and dinner. For the price, which was very reasonable, you cannot beat the Riu Florida Beach. We would DEFINITELY recommend it and stay there again.

<Author>ManchesterUKTraveler
<Content>Nice hotel Cannot quite believe all the negative readings of this hotel. Yes, it does need a little TLC, but it is an older hotel, the lobby is lovely and spacious, the grounds are great as well, and you can walk along the boardwalks in either direction at night, overlooking the sea. You have to be quick to get a poolside lounger, but doesn't that happen all over the world !!! ....we decided to pay the $5 for a lounger on the beach, which was great. We did have quite abit of noise from the road (as our room overlooked the entrance), but it didn't stop us having 10 hours sleep each night !!! Would of probably liked the Hotel to be nearer the action on South Beach, but you pay extra for that, and it can also be quite noiser there. If you drive, the only problem you have is trying to park, but you'll always find somewhere. Valet parking was OK at $9 per night.

<Author>citigorich
<Content>Relaxing Retreat Stayed at the Riu from 3/30 to 4/2... Just got back. I used Trip Advisor for research prior to leaving and here is my summary: Many guests are European, but everyone, American and non blend in well here. The breakfast should be worked into your price of the room - we found the best bargaining with the hotel directly and not the internet travel companies. Grounds were clean and spectacular. Beach was relaxing and water was gorgeous. Staff at the front-desk was friendly - especially the men working there, while the women seemed a tad reserved. The bartenders in and outside were great. Entertainment was worth listening to. Room was updated, balcony was large (but not private), however had an odor - we used nutriair freshner for the room - perhaps something can be done here asap (rug or vent cleanings) - the rooms have poor ventilation (no exhaust fans or screen doors on the balcony). Valet - never had to wait to get the car. Proximity - close to everything, 10 blocks from southbeach and the road to 95 access, and 1 block to the bus. Tips: Bring an air freshner, make friends with the Europeans/South Americans/Americans, get to know your bar tenders/towel staff (Francois)/maid/beach chair guy, 2 blocks south is a discount store with news papers/pool/variety goods and should be used, tip everyone, buy drinks off premises, use breakfast meats and bread for lunch meals, travel to Bayside and take in the free entertainment, listen to the hotel entertainment, dance, have fun.We will be back.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Ignore all the bad reviews. My wife and I just spent three days at the Riu Florida Beach, and I can honestly say to all review readers, definitely ignore all the negative reviews you read about this hotel. Most negative reviews are written by negative-type personalities that find fault with everything that comes into their lives, and in fact their negativity is what draws problems to them. Veteran hotel and service employees can sense this a mile away, and it ultimately affects how they treat you.The hotel has an honest three star rating, and is European flavored through and through. If you want 4 or 5 star, then book it, but this one at three stars is clean, reasonably modern, and presents well. If you want everything perfectly painted, carpetted, decorated, then stick to 5 star hotels, and their prices. 90% of the guests, or what seemed like 90%, were German, French, Italian, etc. The lobby is large and picturesque, the service is good if you smile first, the food is fine (breakfast was included with our room), the pool area is great, and access to the beach and boardwalk is right there. You can take this boardwalk all the way to South Beach if you wanted to.We had booked an oceanfront room, non-smoking, with king size bed, but at check-in we were politely offered a corner room, much larger, but smoking, and after inspection with eyes and nose, we accepted their standard oceanfront non-smoking room. It was bright, clean, and had a great view of the pool, and ocean. We were very comfortable, and had no complaints.The hotel fronts right on Collins Avenue, so the entrance-way seems less than hilton-like, but once into the lobby, everything scales up nicely.The front desk staff were friendly, and all spoke English more or less.The sign said Valet parking $9 per day, but we used it, and were not charged.As another reviewer stated, there is no fitness centre that I could see, but with tons of walking opportunites in either direction, with great ocean views, who would want to jog ten miles on a treadmill, and watch cnn on the t.v. the whole time anyway.If any review readers want to ask questions of my stay at the Riu, please email to gpeter52@yahoo.com thank you.
