<Content>A Riu Dissapointment Don't let the pictures fool you. This place is old, run down, expensive and boring. It has potential but no motivation to make it better. No website, either (just a general one for all Riu properties.. a note to self.. a good hotel will always have a great website)- upon arrival (10 pm) we sat at the pathetic bar in the lobby which was dim and had a disco ball turning slowly, like someone was waiting for a funeral..I ordered a bloody Mary. It was horrific. The bartender simply apolgized that I didin't like it and did not offer to get me something else or take it off my bill.- The room itself is small and tasteless. 2 double beds with cheap linens and musty odor. Cheap towels. NOTHING SPECIAL! Nice view though.- They pride themselves on giving you complimentary chairs and towels at the pool (isn't that a given when you stay somewhere?) and charge $5.00 per chair to lay out on the beach!- There is no life here. No happy hour. The lobby lights were turned down so low most nights, you'd think the hotel was closed.- Food is expensive and not great at all. They charge $15.00 for breakfast, and 20 for dinner (not including gratuity).. it's a big buffet, but there is also a Denny's next door where you can get a grand slam for 6 bucks.- The location is far removed from the action. We walked about 25 blocks everyday to get to the heart of South Beach (one of the reasons we picked this location) to get excercise. - Don't be fooled by it's Only hotel right on the beach selling point. 95 of the hotels on Collins are also right on the beach!- Cabs from there are about 8 bucks each way- One of the elevators was shut down all week (leaving only one working, which took 3-4 minutes everytime, so we ended up climbing stairs most times.- WAY WAY WAY overpriced for what it offers.. Nothing! No gym, no spa, no water sports no attractions or activities.. just an old stuck in a timewarp you don't want to be in.- no good restaurants within close walking distance (maybe 8 blocks or so)- would never recommend this to anyone, and would never come back myself.- The only good thing that happened at Riu was that we (me and my husband) each lost a few pounds from al lthe walking and not eating their food!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Nice Hotel We stayed at the Riu-Miami hotel in January, 2005. Rates were reduced by $20 per night because we were booked into a block of rooms set aside for a wedding. The hotel is lovely and gracious, and the staff tried hard to give us a room ahead of check-in time so our party could change and head for the beach. Although we reserved city view rooms instead of ocean view, we were pleasantly surprised to be given two of the three rooms with ocean view and private patio. The beds were comfortable, but they only offer double beds..no queens or kings. What a bummer. We experienced problems with linens. Cheap, thin, scratchy and never enough. We had to call each day for the correct supply of bath towels, hand towels and wash clothes. Breakfast is included with the rooms. and the food is wonderful and a very nice variety. Hot and cold selections, cereals, fruit, juices, cheeses, nice bread selection...something for everyone. We even saw several older couples preparing sandwiches at their table for enjoyment later in the day. What a deal. Not too much to see in the neighborhood which necessitated our using taxi service to get anywhere. With a party of eight, we had to use two taxis, so it got to be pretty expensive going to dinner and other attractions.

<Author>jmharn
<Content>I just don't get this hotel - So terrible I just got back from this hotel today Feb 1st 2005 after staying there for 6 nights. I try to be as objective as possible so that you guys will find the facts not my opinion.I have stayed in Amerisuites, Comfort Inns, all the way to Ritz Carlton or other high-end hotel chain. Although I have never stayed in a european based hotel, so there is the flaw in my comparison.Here are the facts that I find this hotel is lacking:1. No refrigerator, microwaves, or even coffee maker. If you need coffee in the morning, the hotel restaurant downstair will conveniently pour it for you for a small fee of $2.16 a cup (no refill, nice try). This might be OK for some travelers. But when you have small children this can be a quite inconvenience. Forget warm milk....2. Their welcome booklet says: Tap Water is not drinkable. They do provide a minibar with a bottle water that cost about $3.00 (small one).3. No iron - but they do have a dry cleaning service sheet that I won't even dare to see how much it would cost.4. If you are lucky to stay on 5,7,9th floor you can get to the ice machine on the same floor. Otherwise, you need to wait about 2-3 minutes on the elevator just to get the ice.5. Yes sometimes the elevator does take 3-4 minutes to arrive at certain times of the days (check out times, breakfast, and dinner time). Even the cleaning lady wants to get a piece of the action by crowding the guest elevator too.6. No lotion in the bathroom. Yes, I realize a lot of hotel chains do not give out lotions, but if they call themselves resort - I expect a small bottle of lotion can come in handy especially after a day under the sun.7. The room looks old. This might be subjective, but it does look worn out to me. 8. Oh, if you pay more they do give you a nicer room with balcony (I had that). Here is the lacking part: your neighbor can jump out easily from his balcony to your balcony. There is a dividing wall about waist high. Just enough to hide your head if you sit down - no privacy at all. 9. Related to #8 - the balcony door from the room sticks and DO NOT lock. Now, what's stopping a criminal from the other room to enter your room? Perhaps not much. Oh, but the sunrise, sunset, and the full moon is beautiful from the balcony.10. Pool towel - Make sure you ask for 4 towel cards if you are going to need 4 towels at the pool. Otherwise, the pool tower 'personnel' will give you a hard time for asking more towels than your towel card, as if you are going to steal their prized towel.11. Speaking of towels - so many clean towels that I had got stains on it. I did not even want to think what the stain was from. Just closed my eyes and used them.12. To be fair, some employees are nice, some needs a lesson in cutomer relation (pool towel personnel included). The receptionist with red glasses is nice, the other older one - got a major PMS.13. You cannot check out before your room is completely empty. I just never had that experience. I always check out a bit earlier while my wife is finishing up with the kids. I was confused....Those are facts. I cannot prevent myself from being sarcastic a bit after how they treated us. I just don't get their philosophy. They call themselves a resort, but they are operating a cheap level that I have never seen before even compared to a budget motel. At the same time they pride themselves with their excellent restaurant service (with overpriced everything). I tried their food - mediocre. Not worth spending $25/person.Here is the greatest thing we found about 2 blocks south of the hotel:Cafe Migas. Highly highly recommended. Very modest cafe with excellent cuban coffee and espresso, real orange juice, heavenly ham-and-cheese croissant, full hot breakfast all for under $9. Do yourself a favor don't fall into the hotel's hyped buffet. I read the good and bad reviews about this hotel, and now I believe the bad one. I did not expect a 4 or 5 stars when I got in, but this hotel is lower than 2 star in my humble opinion. Sorry, I have to give my opinion at the end...

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Riu is a great choice when vacationing in South Beach I will admit that despite all of the really GOOD reviews, I was a little apprehensive about the Riu in light of all of the bad reviews. However, much to my satisfaction, we were pleasantly surprised. As expected, we were greeted with 2 glasses of OJ. While I had reserved a room with an ocean view, it was not immediately available upon arrival so we sat outside by the pool at the Alligator Bar and had a few beers. While the bartender needed a course in courtesy training and customer service, he quickly warmed up after giving a tip (servers seem especially appreciative of tips in South Beach). Once we got our room, it was what I expected, nothing fancy, but fine. Pillows could be fluffier and carpet could be replaced, but for $140 a night I was not complaining. Breakfast buffet is great and the lobby and lobby bar are beautiful. The pool and grounds are beautiful and it was great having access to the boardwalk. We also liked the fact that most of the other guests were European, mostly German. All in all, we really enjoyed our stay and the Riu is a BARGAIN! If you like Loews or the Ritz, be prepared to anty up atleast $500 a night. We'll definitely return to the Riu!  
<Date>Nov 12, 2004

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>hotel was average My husband and I stayed here the end of October after having to reschedule a Labor Day trip because of hurricane Jeanne. We were supposed to stay the the Lowes but because of the date change we could not get that hotel for the same price (booked through Expedia). The travel advisor offered the Riu for an additional $6 over what we originally paid along with the $200 airline change fees. We arrived at 1:00 PM and entered a huge lobby that must have been beautiful in its day but it had a very strong cleaning smell that almost made my eyes water. There were 4 people behind the front desk (only 2 were assisting people) and everyone was loudly speaking Spanish. It took 45 minutes to check in. Someone shoved 2 glasses of OJ at us (we were told we would receive a welcome drink at reception) and refused to look at us when we tried to thank them. Anyway, a room was available and we were on our way (only one bellman so we struggled with our bags ourselves).The room was large and comfy but a little run down. Again, the cleaning solution smell was almost overpowering but I was able to open a window for some fresh air. Had a hair dryer and adjustable shower but no coffee maker. There was a mini bar but it only had one beer in it and was never replenished during out 4 night stay.The pool was nice and plenty of chairs to go around at this time of year. The towel/pool person was friendly and helpful. After the weekend the pool water was greasy from suntan lotion - need to have some chemicals so we didn't use it after that. The beach was excellent and the boardwalk is a fun 20 minute walk away from South Beach. The pool bar was a great place to grab lunch. The next closest restaurant is a Denny's that is about 4 city blocks away.Overall our experience with the hotel was ok. When we go back to Miami we will probably go to another hotel.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>If only we would have left sooner Our adventure at the Riu started out great, but went a bit sour. I will try to be as fair about it as possible. We liked what we saw when we got to the lobby. Staff was not overly friendly (aside from a sweetheart of a bellman) but nice enough. The restaurant wasn't open (we got there at 10:30 a.m., so they pointed us to a Denny's down the street.) After we ate, they gave us towel cards and a place to change and store our luggage, but they ended up letting us check in early. We had a very nice ocean front room with a balcony. (I think we had only paid for Ocean view with balcony.) The pool is nice, and the beach is gorgeous and somewhat private. After hanging out by both, we went and sat on our balcony and admired the view. We had a wedding to go to that evening, and on our return was when things got yucky. We came back and there was a huge chunk of the ceiling on the floor of our room (the styrafoam-y type stuff.) We decided to hold off on telling the hotel until the next morning, since it didn't really affect us and we were both tired. We spent a little more time on the balcony, which was again lovely. But when we got back inside, I went to turn off the light in the room, I (barefoot) nearly stepped on one of the hugest cockroaches I have seen (probably two to four inches big). This is Miami, and both the ceiling and the roach can probably be attributed to the humidity, but that didn't make them any more pleasant. My husband called and they said they had no more rooms. He said we can't stay in that room, and they said they would check on some things. They called back with another room and after my husband asked, they said they didn't have a bellman to help us with our now-schlepped together luggage, but sent a security guard with a cart, who looked none too happy, although we did all the work.They put us in a room that reeked of smoke, had no balcony (which we did pay for), looked out onto the street, and was smaller. (Not to mention the fact that I was now afraid to walk on the floor of any of their rooms.) It WAS the middle of the night, so I can understand that options are limited. In the morning we asked to see the manager, and the front desk person asked for the details. She went into the office and then came back and said the manager would be with us. Instead, another employee came out after a few minutes and said the manager was suddenly in a meeting. We explained again and he said we could be in an ocean front room again that night, but we were leaving. My husband said we would like to check out late and have our mini-bar charges (about $8) taken care of. He told us to see him after we ate breakfast, and he was able to give us what we asked for. There were no apologies whatsoever, and it seemed to me that a nice hotel would want to go above and beyond what we asked for (we were very civil about the whole thing), but that was not the case. Anyway, the situation was somewhat rectified, but I would never stay there again or recommend it to anyone, who plans to spend any time in their room. The pool and beach really are great though.  
<Date>Oct 12, 2004

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Awesome stay at the Riu! As soon as my Mom and I arrived at 10:30 a.m., the front desk welcomed us and brought us 2 glasses of orange juice. Inside the room we noticed the smell that was mentioned on previous reviews and the cause of it is HUMIDITY, just turn on A /C and the odor will go away. There were no red insects or bugs. During our 5 days 4 night stay we went to the beach, pool lyed down on the hammock. Went for stroll at the boardwalk (21st-47th street) went to Ocean Drive where restaurants are in South Beach. Check out stores in Lincoln Road on Collins Ave, I believe its 15th or16th street. Take a ferry to see famous homes such as (Rosie O'Donnell or Gloria Estafan all you need to do is take the C or S bus at Indian Creek a block from hotel and get off at Bayside which is in downtown Miami its worth it. The bus fare is $1.25 and on your return back to hotel the bus will leave you in front of Riu on Collins Ave. The breakfast buffet was spectacular, there is a variety of food to please everyone you can sit indoors or outdoors I recommend you sit outside to take the morning breeze, sun and the view of the pool. On a daily basis the housecleaning maid left us nicely decorated towels in a shape of heart, butterfly, two swans. Overall I can't complain about this hotel, twice the front desk called to see if I had any problems/issues and I had none. I'm glad we went despite the negative reviews that we read. Go for it and enjoy your stay in Riu!!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Where did these negative people stay? My wife and I stayed at the Riu for one night prior to a Cruise on the Carnival Triumph and for a further seven days after the cruise. We found the Hotel exactly as described in the brochures and their on-line advertising and really cannot understand some of the negative reviews we read previous to our stay. Let me assure you that my wife and I are not easily impressed with hotel accommodation, having stayed in many 4 and five star hotels worldwide, and while it is true that the staff at the Riu are Spanish speakers who sometimes lost a little in translating our English, we found them very helpful and friendly. The breakfast buffet is superb, and though we chose to eat out in the evenings taking a short cab ride into the town centre, the food on display for the evening buffet looked excellent. The cost of the buffet was $16 to $18 + tax which I consider very cheap considering the fact that if you were a big eater (which we are not) you could eat as much as you could carry on your plate and then return for more. As far as musty smells are concerned, we noticed none of that on our first night, but when we returned the only room available with the view we required was a smoking room and did smell musty for a day or so, until the room had been aired and then there was no problem. The rooms we occupied were spotless and the maid service excellent. I spent a lot of time walkin the boardwalks NJorth and South, and the pool and gardens of thew Riu were the best I saw apart from the Fontainbleu Hilton which is a serious five star and nearly three times as expensive.The two lifts are a little slow if you consider having to wait 90 seconds on average for service, but if you are on holiday and get stressed by that you seriously should consider getting a life.If not and you are thinking of staying there, Do it!. you will not be dissapointed, it is a superb value for money hotel and we will definitely stay there again when in Miami.  
<Date>May 8, 2004

<Author>Saralondon
<Content>Fantastic pool area but far from the center of town As one of the cheaper hotels in South Beach, The Riu Florida is excellent value for money. The pool area is gorgeous, buffet breakfast is great, rooms comfortable and air-conditioned and the hotel is literally right on the beach. The only downside is that the hotel is a $6-$7 cab journey from Ocean Drive, the center of South Beach. The service is also not that great or friendly, but I found that to be true of the whole of Miami in general. Overall, this hotel is a great place to stay.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>There are other hotels on Collin's Avenue Following a luxury cruise on the 'Explorer of the Seas' my family and I spent a couple of nights at the 'Riu' which I booked over the internet. Did I do right?? Location:-Superb - backs onto South Miami Beach - but beware, chairs on the beach cost $5 and umbrellas $10 to hire. Rather expensive for a family of four. Hotel:-No air coditioning in our room just a ceiling fan. Our room o/k but drab and dingy. No tea/coffee machine in room, no writting materials and no red beetles! Dining Room:-food was fine but we paid the price for it. The $16 buffet dinner turned out to cost more than stated. No iced water could be served with the meal, bottled wter only in the Dining Room, at a price. Bills for meals and drinks were seperate which meant two service charges and two state taxes at 7%. taking the bill to around $48 each. Hotel souvenir shop:- selection of souvenirs very sparse when the shop was actually open. Shops about 6 blocks south. Some other reviewer mentioned Denny's, stick to their coffee if you must. Bus takes 25 minutes to get to shopping Mall, clothing very highly priced. Better prices and bargains on streets inland from Intercontinental Hotel. Plus points - beach, hotel pool and gardens and being in Miami. Minus points - musty smell in corridors and room, staff not too attentive. Hotel statement:- Delux Hotel questionable - Completly refurbished what year? Minutes from fine dining and shops by what form of transport? helicoter, Harley, Liar jet? Conclusion - Would I stay again - No - You could do better booking into another Collins Avenue hotel.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Riu OK for one or 2 nights Stayed at the Riu on January 11, 2004 for one night. The hotel lobby and pool were better than average, the hotel room was average and just consisted of a necessities, a bed, and a bathroom (no separate living room area). We did not see any evidence of bugs or dirty rooms, and slept comfortably, I probably would not spend a week there. The staff was friendly and the breakfast buffet was great. Found out that if you pre-pay for your room through a discount website like hotels the breakfast is an extra $15.00. Since I did our reservations through freehotelguide and did not prepay, we were entitled to the breakfast buffet for free. If you don't like spending $15.00 on breakfast, there is a Denny's down the street. Overall I was pleased with my stay at the Riu and would stay there again if only for one or 2 nights.

<Author>Cancan
<Content>Has potential but management is inefficient Staying in this hotel will make you think you are in a foreign country. While the rooms are adequate (though need refurbishing) and the staffs are friendly, the hotel management style will remind you of the inefficiencies of layback countries. Since we just came back from the south of Spain we weren't too surprise or disappointed. The operator answering the hotel 'front desk phone' does not speak or comprehend English, at all. The 'hotel concierge' also plays another role as the hotel convenient store shopkeeper so there is a long wait to be served. The receptionists behind the front desk have good intentions but they are untrained and unfamiliar with standard American hotel practice. If you don't understand their culture you would call their management style 'unprofessional'. So, avoid needing help from the hotel and you would enjoy your stay in Riu Florida Beach.
